<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> are the two largest parties in the state. A plurality of voters are registered as undeclared, and can choose either ballot in the primary and then regain their undeclared status after voting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_(United_States)" title="Libertarian Party (United States)">Libertarian Party</a> had official party status from 1990 to 1996, and has a program known as the <a href="/wiki/Free_State_Project" title="Free State Project">Free State Project</a> with the goal of turning New Hampshire into a libertarian stronghold by suggesting that libertarians move there so they can concentrate their power. The <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_of_New_Hampshire" title="Libertarian Party of New Hampshire">Libertarian Party</a> regained ballot access after the 2016 election because the gubernatorial candidate received over 4% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of February 5, 2016, there were 882,959 registered voters, of whom 389,472 (44.1%) did not declare a political party affiliation, 262,111 (29.7%) were Republican, and 231,376 (26.2%) were Democratic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Hampshire_primary">New Hampshire primary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: New Hampshire primary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2536" data-file-width="3895" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg/220px-Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg/330px-Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg/440px-Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alumni_Hall_1889_Sun.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Saint_Anselm_College" title="Saint Anselm College">Saint Anselm College</a> has held several national debates on campus.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New Hampshire is internationally known for the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_primary" title="New Hampshire primary">New Hampshire primary</a>, the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_primary" title="U.S. presidential primary">primary</a> in the quadrennial American presidential election cycle. State law requires that the Secretary of State schedule this election at least one week before any "similar event." However, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iowa_caucus" title="Iowa caucus">Iowa caucus</a> has preceded the New Hampshire primary. This primary, as the nation's first contest that uses the same procedure as the general election, draws more attention than those in other states, and has often been decisive in shaping the national contest.</p>
<p>State law permits a town with fewer than 100 residents to open its polls at midnight, and close when all registered citizens have cast their ballots. As such, the communities of <a href="/wiki/Dixville_Notch,_New_Hampshire" title="Dixville Notch, New Hampshire">Dixville Notch</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coos_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Coos County, New Hampshire">Coos County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hart%27s_Location,_New_Hampshire" title="Hart's Location, New Hampshire">Hart's Location</a> in <a href="/wiki/Carroll_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Carroll County, New Hampshire">Carroll County</a>, among others, have chosen to implement these provisions. Dixville Notch and Hart's Location are traditionally the first places in both New Hampshire and the U.S. to vote in presidential primaries and elections.</p>
<p>Nominations for all other partisan offices are decided in a separate <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">primary election</a>. In Presidential election cycles, this is the second primary election held in New Hampshire.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saint_Anselm_College" title="Saint Anselm College">Saint Anselm College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Goffstown,_New_Hampshire" title="Goffstown, New Hampshire">Goffstown</a> has become a popular campaign spot for politicians as well as several national presidential debates because of its proximity to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester-Boston_Regional_Airport" title="Manchester-Boston Regional Airport">Manchester-Boston Regional Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_results">Election results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Election results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the past, New Hampshire has often voted Republican. Between 1856 and 1988, New Hampshire cast its electoral votes for the Democratic presidential ticket six times: <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> (twice), <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> (three times), and <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> (once).</p>
<p>Beginning in 1992, New Hampshire became a <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a> in both national and local elections. The state supported Democrats <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> in 1992 and 1996, <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> in 2004, and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2008 and 2012. It was the only state in the country to switch from supporting Republican <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2000" title="United States presidential election, 2000">2000 election</a> to supporting his Democratic challenger in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2004" title="United States presidential election, 2004">2004 election</a>, when <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, a senator from neighboring Massachusetts, won the state. <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> very narrowly lost the state in 2016.</p>
<p>The Democrats dominated elections in New Hampshire in 2006 and 2008. In 2006, Democrats won both congressional seats (electing <a href="/wiki/Carol_Shea-Porter" title="Carol Shea-Porter">Carol Shea-Porter</a> in the 1st district and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hodes" title="Paul Hodes">Paul Hodes</a> in the 2nd district), re-elected Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Lynch_(New_Hampshire)" title="John Lynch (New Hampshire)">John Lynch</a>, and gained a majority on the Executive Council and in both houses of the legislature for the first time since 1911. Democrats had not held both the legislature and the governorship since 1874.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Neither U.S. Senate seat was up for a vote in 2006. In 2008, Democrats retained their majorities, governorship, and Congressional seats; and former governor <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_Shaheen" title="Jeanne Shaheen">Jeanne Shaheen</a> defeated incumbent Republican <a href="/wiki/John_E._Sununu" title="John E. Sununu">John E. Sununu</a> for the U.S. Senate in a rematch of the 2002 contest.</p>
<p>The 2008 elections resulted in women holding a majority, 13 of the 24 seats, in the New Hampshire Senate, a first for any legislative body in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2010 midterm elections, Republicans made historic gains in New Hampshire, capturing veto-proof majorities in the state legislature, taking all five seats in the Executive Council, electing a new U.S. senator, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Ayotte" title="Kelly Ayotte">Kelly Ayotte</a>, winning both U.S. House seats, and reducing the margin of victory of incumbent Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Lynch_(New_Hampshire)" title="John Lynch (New Hampshire)">John Lynch</a> compared to his 2006 and 2008 landslide wins.</p>
<p>In the 2012 state legislative elections, Democrats took back the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_House_of_Representatives" title="New Hampshire House of Representatives">New Hampshire House of Representatives</a> and narrowed the Republican majority in the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Senate" title="New Hampshire Senate">New Hampshire Senate</a> to 13-11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In 2012, New Hampshire became the first state in U.S. history to elect an all-female federal delegation: Democratic Congresswomen <a href="/wiki/Carol_Shea-Porter" title="Carol Shea-Porter">Carol Shea-Porter</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="New Hampshire's 1st congressional district">Congressional District 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ann_McLane_Kuster" title="Ann McLane Kuster">Ann McLane Kuster</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="New Hampshire's 2nd congressional district">Congressional District 2</a> accompanied U.S. Senators <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_Shaheen" title="Jeanne Shaheen">Jeanne Shaheen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Ayotte" title="Kelly Ayotte">Kelly Ayotte</a> in 2013. Further, the state elected its second female governor: Democrat <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Hassan" title="Maggie Hassan">Maggie Hassan</a>.</p>
<p>In the 2014 elections, Republicans retook the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_House_of_Representatives" title="New Hampshire House of Representatives">New Hampshire House of Representatives</a> with a 239-160 majority and expanded their majority in the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Senate" title="New Hampshire Senate">New Hampshire Senate</a> to 14 of the Senate's 24 seats. On the national level, incumbent Democratic Senator <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_Shaheen" title="Jeanne Shaheen">Jeanne Shaheen</a> defeated her Republican challenger, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Brown_(politician)" title="Scott Brown (politician)">Scott Brown</a>. New Hampshire also elected <a href="/wiki/Frank_Guinta" title="Frank Guinta">Frank Guinta</a> (R) for its First Congressional District representative and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ann_Kuster" title="Ann Kuster">Ann Kuster</a> (D) for its Second Congressional District representative.</p>
<p>In the 2016 elections, Republicans held the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_House_of_Representatives" title="New Hampshire House of Representatives">New Hampshire House of Representatives</a> with a reduced majority of 220-175, and held onto their 14 seats in the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Senate" title="New Hampshire Senate">New Hampshire Senate</a>. On the national level, incumbent Republican Senator <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Ayotte" title="Kelly Ayotte">Kelly Ayotte</a> was defeated by Democratic challenger, Governor <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Hassan" title="Maggie Hassan">Maggie Hassan</a>, by a plurality of 978 votes, or 0.1%, meaning that Hassan became the first Democrat to hold that Senate seat since <a href="/wiki/John_A._Durkin" title="John A. Durkin">John A. Durkin</a> was defeated in 1980 by <a href="/wiki/Warren_Rudman" title="Warren Rudman">Warren Rudman</a>. <a href="/wiki/Frank_Guinta" title="Frank Guinta">Frank Guinta</a>, the representative for <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="New Hampshire's 1st congressional district">Congressional District 1</a> was defeated once again by <a href="/wiki/Carol_Shea-Porter" title="Carol Shea-Porter">Carol Shea-Porter</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Ann_McLane_Kuster" title="Ann McLane Kuster">Ann McLane Kuster</a>, the representative for <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="New Hampshire's 2nd congressional district">Congressional District 2</a> was re-elected, meaning that, with incumbent Senator <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_Shaheen" title="Jeanne Shaheen">Jeanne Shaheen</a>, New Hampshire became the first state to send an all-female, all-Democratic congressional delegation to Washington, D.C. In the gubernatorial race, retiring Governor <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Hassan" title="Maggie Hassan">Maggie Hassan</a> was succeeded by Republican <a href="/wiki/Chris_Sununu" title="Chris Sununu">Chris Sununu</a>, who defeated Democratic nominee <a href="/wiki/Colin_Van_Ostern" title="Colin Van Ostern">Colin Van Ostern</a>. Sununu became the state's first Republican governor since <a href="/wiki/Craig_Benson" title="Craig Benson">Craig Benson</a>, who left office in 2005 following defeat by <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/John_Lynch" title="John Lynch">John Lynch</a>. In the presidential race, the state voted for the Democratic nominee, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State" title="Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> over the Republican nominee, Donald Trump, by a margin of 2,687 votes, or 0.4%, one of the closest results the state has ever seen in a presidential race.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_State_Project">Free State Project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Free State Project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Free_State_Project" title="Free State Project">Free State Project</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Free_State_Project" title="Free State Project">Free State Project</a> seeks to entice 20,000 individuals with libertarian-leaning views to move to New Hampshire with the intent of reducing the size and scope of government at the local, state and federal levels through active participation in the political process. On February 3, 2016, the project reached its goal of 20,000 signers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The Free State Project holds the annual <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Liberty_Forum" title="New Hampshire Liberty Forum">New Hampshire Liberty Forum</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and the annual Porcupine Freedom Festival, also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PorcFest" title="PorcFest">PorcFest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>New Hampshire has a well-maintained, well-signed network of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_highways" title="Interstate highways">Interstate highways</a>, U.S. highways, and state highways. State highway markers still depict the <a href="/wiki/Old_Man_of_the_Mountain" title="Old Man of the Mountain">Old Man of the Mountain</a> despite that rock formation's demise in 2003. Several route numbers align with the same route numbers in neighboring states. State highway numbering does not indicate the highway's direction. Major routes include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I-89.svg"><img alt="I-89.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/I-89.svg/20px-I-89.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/I-89.svg/30px-I-89.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/I-89.svg/40px-I-89.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_89" title="Interstate 89">Interstate 89</a> runs northwest from near <a href="/wiki/Concord,_New_Hampshire" title="Concord, New Hampshire">Concord</a> to <a href="/wiki/Lebanon,_New_Hampshire" title="Lebanon, New Hampshire">Lebanon</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> border.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I-93.svg"><img alt="I-93.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/I-93.svg/20px-I-93.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/I-93.svg/30px-I-93.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/I-93.svg/40px-I-93.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_93" title="Interstate 93">Interstate 93</a> is the main Interstate highway in New Hampshire and runs north from <a href="/wiki/Salem,_New_Hampshire" title="Salem, New Hampshire">Salem</a> (on the Massachusetts border) to <a href="/wiki/Littleton,_New_Hampshire" title="Littleton, New Hampshire">Littleton</a> (on the Vermont border). I-93 connects the more densely populated southern part of the state to the Lakes Region and the White Mountains further to the north.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I-95.svg"><img alt="I-95.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/I-95.svg/20px-I-95.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/I-95.svg/30px-I-95.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/I-95.svg/40px-I-95.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a> runs north–south briefly along New Hampshire's seacoast to serve the city of <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_New_Hampshire" title="Portsmouth, New Hampshire">Portsmouth</a>, before entering <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_1.svg"><img alt="US 1.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/US_1.svg/20px-US_1.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/US_1.svg/30px-US_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/US_1.svg/40px-US_1.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1" title="U.S. Route 1">U.S. Route 1</a> runs north–south briefly along New Hampshire's seacoast to the east of and paralleling I-95.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_2.svg"><img alt="US 2.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/US_2.svg/20px-US_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/US_2.svg/30px-US_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/US_2.svg/40px-US_2.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_2" title="U.S. Route 2">U.S. Route 2</a> runs east–west through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coos_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Coos County, New Hampshire">Coos County</a> from Maine, intersecting <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Route_16" title="New Hampshire Route 16">Route 16</a>, skirting the <a href="/wiki/White_Mountain_National_Forest" title="White Mountain National Forest">White Mountain National Forest</a> passing through <a href="/wiki/Jefferson,_New_Hampshire" title="Jefferson, New Hampshire">Jefferson</a> and into Vermont.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_3.svg"><img alt="US 3.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/US_3.svg/20px-US_3.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/US_3.svg/30px-US_3.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/US_3.svg/40px-US_3.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_3" title="U.S. Route 3">U.S. Route 3</a> is the longest numbered route in the state, and the only one to run completely through the state from the Massachusetts border to the Canada–US border. It generally parallels <a href="/wiki/Interstate_93" title="Interstate 93">Interstate 93</a>. South of Manchester, it takes a more westerly route through <a href="/wiki/Nashua,_New_Hampshire" title="Nashua, New Hampshire">Nashua</a>. North of Franconia Notch, U.S. 3 takes a more easterly route, before terminating at the Canada–US border.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_4.svg"><img alt="US 4.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/US_4.svg/20px-US_4.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/US_4.svg/30px-US_4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/US_4.svg/40px-US_4.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_4" title="U.S. Route 4">U.S. Route 4</a> terminates at the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Traffic_Circle" title="Portsmouth Traffic Circle">Portsmouth Traffic Circle</a> and runs east–west across the southern part of the state connecting <a href="/wiki/Durham,_New_Hampshire" title="Durham, New Hampshire">Durham</a>, Concord, <a href="/wiki/Boscawen,_New_Hampshire" title="Boscawen, New Hampshire">Boscawen</a> and Lebanon.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NH_Route_16.svg"><img alt="NH Route 16.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/NH_Route_16.svg/20px-NH_Route_16.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/NH_Route_16.svg/30px-NH_Route_16.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/NH_Route_16.svg/40px-NH_Route_16.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Route_16" title="New Hampshire Route 16">New Hampshire Route 16</a> is a major north–south highway in the eastern part of the state that generally parallels the border with <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, eventually entering Maine as Maine Route 16. The southernmost portion of NH 16 is a four-lane freeway, co-signed with U.S. Route 4.</li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NH_Route_101.svg"><img alt="NH Route 101.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/NH_Route_101.svg/20px-NH_Route_101.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/NH_Route_101.svg/30px-NH_Route_101.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/NH_Route_101.svg/40px-NH_Route_101.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a> <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Route_101" title="New Hampshire Route 101">New Hampshire Route 101</a> is a major east–west highway in the southern part of the state that connects <a href="/wiki/Keene,_New_Hampshire" title="Keene, New Hampshire">Keene</a> with <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester</a> and the Seacoast region. East of Manchester, NH 101 is a four-lane, limited access highway that runs to <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Beach,_New_Hampshire" title="Hampton Beach, New Hampshire">Hampton Beach</a> and I-95.</li>
</ul>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Highway_System" title="New Hampshire Highway System">New Hampshire Highway System</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>New Hampshire has 25 public-use airports, three with some scheduled commercial passenger service. The busiest airport by number of passengers handled is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester-Boston_Regional_Airport" title="Manchester-Boston Regional Airport">Manchester-Boston Regional Airport</a> in Manchester and <a href="/wiki/Londonderry,_New_Hampshire" title="Londonderry, New Hampshire">Londonderry</a>, which serves the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Greater Boston</a> metropolitan area.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_New_Hampshire" title="List of airports in New Hampshire">List of airports in New Hampshire</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">Public transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Long-distance intercity passenger rail service is provided by <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Vermonter_(train)" title="Vermonter (train)">Vermonter</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Downeaster_(train)" title="Downeaster (train)">Downeaster</a></i> lines.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concord_Coach_Lines" title="Concord Coach Lines">Concord Coach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vermont_Translines" title="Vermont Translines">Vermont Translines</a> and Dartmouth Coach all provide intercity bus connections to and from points in New Hampshire and to long-distance points beyond and in between.</p>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Boston-centered <a href="/wiki/MBTA_Commuter_Rail" title="MBTA Commuter Rail">MBTA Commuter Rail</a> services reach only as far as northern Massachusetts. The <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Rail_Transit_Authority" title="New Hampshire Rail Transit Authority">New Hampshire Rail Transit Authority</a> is working to extend "Capital Corridor" service from <a href="/wiki/Lowell,_Massachusetts" title="Lowell, Massachusetts">Lowell, Massachusetts</a>, to Nashua, Concord, and Manchester, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester-Boston_Regional_Airport" title="Manchester-Boston Regional Airport">Manchester-Boston Regional Airport</a>; and "Coastal Corridor" service from <a href="/wiki/Haverhill,_Massachusetts" title="Haverhill, Massachusetts">Haverhill, Massachusetts</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Plaistow,_New_Hampshire" title="Plaistow, New Hampshire">Plaistow, New Hampshire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Legislation in 2007 created the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Rail_Transit_Authority" title="New Hampshire Rail Transit Authority">New Hampshire Rail Transit Authority</a> (NHRTA) with the goal of overseeing the development of commuter rail in the state of New Hampshire. In 2011, Governor John Lynch vetoed HB 218, a bill passed by Republican lawmakers, which would have drastically curtailed the powers and responsibilities of NHRTA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The I-93 Corridor transit study suggested a rail alternative along the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_and_Lawrence_Railroad" title="Manchester and Lawrence Railroad">Manchester and Lawrence branch line</a> which could provide freight and passenger service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> This rail corridor would also have access to Manchester-Boston Regional Airport.</p>
<p>Eleven public transit authorities operate local and regional bus services around the state, and eight private carriers operate express bus services which link with the national intercity bus network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhdotrs_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-nhdotrs-73">[73]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Department_of_Transportation" title="New Hampshire Department of Transportation">New Hampshire Department of Transportation</a> operates a statewide ride-sharing match service, in addition to independent ride matching and guaranteed ride home programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhdotrs_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-nhdotrs-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourist_railroad" title="Tourist railroad">Tourist railroads</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Conway_Scenic_Railroad" title="Conway Scenic Railroad">Conway Scenic Railroad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hobo-Winnipesaukee_Railroad" title="Hobo-Winnipesaukee Railroad">Hobo-Winnipesaukee Railroad</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington_Cog_Railway" title="Mount Washington Cog Railway">Mount Washington Cog Railway</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight_railways">Freight railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Freight railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Freight railways in New Hampshire include <a href="/wiki/Concord_and_Claremont_Railroad" title="Concord and Claremont Railroad">Claremont &amp; Concord Railroad</a> (CCRR), <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Railways" title="Pan Am Railways">Pan Am Railways</a> via subsidiary Springfield Terminal Railway (ST), the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Central_Railroad" title="New England Central Railroad">New England Central Railroad</a> (NHCR), the <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_and_Atlantic_Railroad" title="St. Lawrence and Atlantic Railroad">St. Lawrence and Atlantic Railroad</a> (SLR), and <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Northcoast_Corporation" title="New Hampshire Northcoast Corporation">New Hampshire Northcoast Corporation</a> (NHN).</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_Hampshire_railroads" title="List of New Hampshire railroads">List of New Hampshire railroads</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_schools">High schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: High schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_New_Hampshire" title="List of high schools in New Hampshire">List of high schools in New Hampshire</a></div>
<p>The first public high schools in the state were the Boys' High School and the Girls' High School of <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_New_Hampshire" title="Portsmouth, New Hampshire">Portsmouth</a>, established either in 1827 or 1830 depending on the source.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>New Hampshire has more than 80 public high schools, many of which serve more than one town. The largest is <a href="/wiki/Pinkerton_Academy" title="Pinkerton Academy">Pinkerton Academy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Derry,_New_Hampshire" title="Derry, New Hampshire">Derry</a>, which is owned by a private non-profit organization and serves as the public high school of a number of neighboring towns. There are at least 30 private high schools in the state.</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.nh.gov/residents/k12.html" rel="nofollow">New Hampshire public schools with a Web presence</a></li>
</ul>
<p>In 2008 the state tied with Massachusetts as having the highest scores on the SAT and ACT standardized tests given to high school students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>

</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following professional and professional development sports teams are located in New Hampshire:</p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Motor_Speedway" title="New Hampshire Motor Speedway">New Hampshire Motor Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Loudon,_New_Hampshire" title="Loudon, New Hampshire">Loudon</a> is an oval track and road course which has been visited by national motorsport championship series such as the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a>, the NASCAR <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationwide_Series" title="Nationwide Series">Nationwide Series</a>, the NASCAR <a href="/wiki/Camping_World_Truck_Series" title="Camping World Truck Series">Camping World Truck Series</a>, NASCAR <a href="/wiki/Whelen_Modified_Tour" title="Whelen Modified Tour">Whelen Modified Tour</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Canadian_Tour" title="American Canadian Tour">American Canadian Tour</a> (ACT), the <a href="/wiki/Champ_Car" title="Champ Car">Champ Car</a> and the <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a>. Other motor racing venues include <a href="/wiki/Star_Speedway" title="Star Speedway">Star Speedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England_Dragway" title="New England Dragway">New England Dragway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Epping,_New_Hampshire" title="Epping, New Hampshire">Epping</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lee_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lee Speedway (page does not exist)">Lee Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lee,_New_Hampshire" title="Lee, New Hampshire">Lee</a>, Twin State Speedway in <a href="/wiki/Claremont,_New_Hampshire" title="Claremont, New Hampshire">Claremont</a>, Monadnock Speedway in <a href="/wiki/Winchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Winchester, New Hampshire">Winchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canaan_Motor_Club" title="Canaan Motor Club">Canaan Fair Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canaan,_New_Hampshire" title="Canaan, New Hampshire">Canaan</a>.</p>
<p>New Hampshire has two <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> teams: the <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_Big_Green" title="Dartmouth Big Green">Dartmouth Big Green</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Wildcats" title="New Hampshire Wildcats">New Hampshire Wildcats</a> (<a href="/wiki/America_East_Conference" title="America East Conference">America East Conference</a>), as well as three Division II teams: Franklin Pierce Ravens, Saint Anselm Hawks and Southern New Hampshire Penmen (<a href="/wiki/Northeast-10_Conference" title="Northeast-10 Conference">Northeast-10 Conference</a>).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seacoast_United_Phantoms" title="Seacoast United Phantoms">Seacoast United Phantoms</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_New_Hampshire" title="Portsmouth, New Hampshire">Portsmouth</a>. Founded in 1996, the team plays in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USL_Premier_Development_League" title="USL Premier Development League">USL Premier Development League</a> (PDL), the fourth tier of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Soccer_Pyramid" title="American Soccer Pyramid">American Soccer Pyramid</a>, in the Northeast Division of the Eastern Conference. The team plays its home games in the stadium on the campus of <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_High_School_(New_Hampshire)" title="Portsmouth High School (New Hampshire)">Portsmouth High School</a>, where they have played since 2011.</p>
<p>Annually since 2002, high-school statewide all-stars compete against Vermont in ten sports during "Twin State" playoffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the spring, New Hampshire's many <a href="/wiki/Sugar_house" title="Sugar house">sap houses</a> hold sugaring-off open houses. In summer and early autumn, New Hampshire is home to many <a href="/wiki/Fair" title="Fair">county fairs</a>, the largest being the <a href="/wiki/Hopkinton_State_Fair" title="Hopkinton State Fair">Hopkinton State Fair</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Contoocook,_New_Hampshire" title="Contoocook, New Hampshire">Contoocook</a>. New Hampshire's <a href="/wiki/Lakes_Region_(New_Hampshire)" title="Lakes Region (New Hampshire)">Lakes Region</a> is home to many summer camps, especially around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipesaukee" title="Lake Winnipesaukee">Lake Winnipesaukee</a>, and is a popular tourist destination. The Peterborough Players have performed every summer in <a href="/wiki/Peterborough,_New_Hampshire" title="Peterborough, New Hampshire">Peterborough, New Hampshire</a> since 1933. The <a href="/wiki/Barnstormers_Theatre" title="Barnstormers Theatre">Barnstormers Theatre</a> in Tamworth, New Hampshire, founded in 1931, is one of the longest-running professional summer theaters in the United States. In the fall New Hampshire is host to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highland_Games" title="Highland Games">New Hampshire Highland Games</a>. New Hampshire has also registered an official <a href="/wiki/Tartan" title="Tartan">tartan</a> with the proper authorities in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, used to make kilts worn by the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_New_Hampshire" title="Lincoln, New Hampshire">Lincoln</a> Police Department while its officers serve during the games. The <a href="/wiki/Autumn_leaf_color" title="Autumn leaf color">fall foliage</a> peaks in mid-October. In the winter, <a href="/wiki/List_of_ski_areas_and_resorts_in_the_United_States#New_Hampshire" title="List of ski areas and resorts in the United States">New Hampshire's ski areas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snowmobile" title="Snowmobile">snowmobile</a> trails attract visitors from a wide area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> After the lakes freeze over they become dotted with <a href="/wiki/Ice_fishing" title="Ice fishing">ice fishing</a> ice houses, known locally as bobhouses. <a href="/wiki/Funspot_Family_Fun_Center" title="Funspot Family Fun Center">Funspot</a>, the world's largest video arcade<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (now termed a museum), is located in <a href="/wiki/Laconia,_New_Hampshire" title="Laconia, New Hampshire">Laconia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_fiction">In fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: In fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comics">Comics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Comics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>Bob Montana, the original artist for <a href="/wiki/Archie_Comics" title="Archie Comics"><i>Archie</i> Comics</a>, attended <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Central_High_School" title="Manchester Central High School">Manchester Central High School</a> for a year, and may have based Riverdale High School in part on Central.</li>
<li>Al Capp, creator of the comic strip <i><a href="/wiki/Li%27l_Abner" title="Li'l Abner">Li'l Abner</a></i>, used to joke that <a href="/wiki/Dogpatch" title="Dogpatch">Dogpatch</a>, the setting for the strip, was based on <a href="/wiki/Seabrook,_New_Hampshire" title="Seabrook, New Hampshire">Seabrook</a>, where he would vacation with his wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Separate_Peace_(film)" title="A Separate Peace (film)">A Separate Peace</a></i> (1972) was filmed in <a href="/wiki/Exeter,_New_Hampshire" title="Exeter, New Hampshire">Exeter</a> at <a href="/wiki/Phillips_Exeter_Academy" title="Phillips Exeter Academy">Phillips Exeter Academy</a>, alma mater of author <a href="/wiki/John_Knowles" title="John Knowles">John Knowles</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Animal_House" title="Animal House">Animal House</a></i> (1978) is said to be inspired by <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a>, alma mater of one of the scriptwriters, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Miller_(writer)" title="Chris Miller (writer)">Chris Miller</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/On_Golden_Pond_(1981_film)" title="On Golden Pond (1981 film)">On Golden Pond</a></i> (1981) was filmed and takes place at <a href="/wiki/Squam_Lake" title="Squam Lake">Squam Lake</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_World_According_to_Garp_(film)" title="The World According to Garp (film)">The World According to Garp</a></i> (1982), although filmed elsewhere, is set in a thinly disguised Phillips Exeter, alma mater of author <a href="/wiki/John_Irving" title="John Irving">John Irving</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/What_About_Bob%3F" title="What About Bob?">What About Bob?</a></i> (1991) takes place primarily at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipesaukee" title="Lake Winnipesaukee">Lake Winnipesaukee</a> but was actually filmed in Virginia.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Jumanji" title="Jumanji">Jumanji</a></i> (1995) was filmed in <a href="/wiki/Keene,_New_Hampshire" title="Keene, New Hampshire">Keene</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/In_Dreams_(film)" title="In Dreams (film)">In Dreams</a></i> (1999) had location shots filmed in <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_New_Hampshire" title="New Castle, New Hampshire">New Castle</a>, showing a ghostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wentworth-by-the-Sea_Hotel" title="Wentworth-by-the-Sea Hotel">Wentworth-by-the-Sea Hotel</a> before its restoration.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Live_Free_or_Die_(2006_film)" title="Live Free or Die (2006 film)">Live Free or Die</a></i> (2006) was filmed in <a href="/wiki/Claremont,_New_Hampshire" title="Claremont, New Hampshire">Claremont</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/In_Your_Eyes_(2014_film)" title="In Your Eyes (2014 film)">In Your Eyes</a></i> (2014) was primarily shot in New Hampshire and partially takes place in Exeter and <a href="/wiki/Hooksett,_New_Hampshire" title="Hooksett, New Hampshire">Hooksett</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Many novels, plays and screenplays have been set in New Hampshire. The state has played other roles in fiction, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>New Hampshire born <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Webster" title="Daniel Webster">Daniel Webster</a> is a prominent figure in <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Vincent_Ben%C3%A9t" title="Stephen Vincent Benét">Stephen Vincent Benét</a>'s short story entitled "<a href="/wiki/The_Devil_and_Daniel_Webster" title="The Devil and Daniel Webster">The Devil and Daniel Webster</a>" (1937), about a New Hampshire farmer who sells his soul to the devil and is defended by Daniel Webster.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peterborough,_New_Hampshire" title="Peterborough, New Hampshire">Peterborough</a> is the inspiration for the town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grover%27s_Corners" title="Grover's Corners">Grover's Corners</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Wilder" title="Thornton Wilder">Thornton Wilder</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/Our_Town" title="Our Town">Our Town</a> (1938)</i>.</li>
<li>The novel <i><a href="/wiki/Peyton_Place_(novel)" title="Peyton Place (novel)">Peyton Place</a></i> (1956) was inspired by the town of <a href="/wiki/Gilmanton,_New_Hampshire" title="Gilmanton, New Hampshire">Gilmanton</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Knowles" title="John Knowles">John Knowles</a> based the Devon School in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Separate_Peace" title="A Separate Peace">A Separate Peace</a></i> (1959) on <a href="/wiki/Phillips_Exeter_Academy" title="Phillips Exeter Academy">Phillips Exeter Academy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Exeter,_New_Hampshire" title="Exeter, New Hampshire">Exeter</a>.</li>
<li>The prep school in <a href="/wiki/John_Irving" title="John Irving">John Irving</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_According_to_Garp" title="The World According to Garp">The World According to Garp</a></i> (1978) was also based on Phillips Exeter Academy. Irving's stepfather was a faculty member at the school, and Irving is an alumnus; New Hampshire settings are common in his works, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hotel_New_Hampshire" title="The Hotel New Hampshire">The Hotel New Hampshire</a></i> (1981).</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>In the cable television series <i><a href="/wiki/Breaking_Bad" title="Breaking Bad">Breaking Bad</a></i>, the character <a href="/wiki/Walter_White_(Breaking_Bad)" title="Walter White (Breaking Bad)">Walter White</a> escapes to a cabin in a fictional county in Northern New Hampshire, and two of the show's episodes are titled "<a href="/wiki/Live_Free_or_Die_(Breaking_Bad)" title="Live Free or Die (Breaking Bad)">Live Free or Die</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Granite_State_(Breaking_Bad)" title="Granite State (Breaking Bad)">Granite State</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">The Sopranos</a></i> episode, "<a href="/wiki/Live_Free_or_Die_(The_Sopranos)" title="Live Free or Die (The Sopranos)">Live Free or Die</a>", the character <a href="/wiki/Vito_Spatafore" title="Vito Spatafore">Vito Spatafore</a> hides out, for a time, from the New Jersey and New York mob families in New Hampshire.</li>
<li>The character of <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Bartlet" title="Josiah Bartlet">Josiah Bartlet</a>, President of the United States on the television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i>, was depicted as a two-term New Hampshire governor.</li>
<li>In the television show <a href="/wiki/Gilmore_Girls" title="Gilmore Girls">Gilmore Girls</a>, characters Rory and Lorelai stay at a bed and breakfast in <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_New_Hampshire" title="Portsmouth, New Hampshire">Portsmouth, New Hampshire</a>, in the episode "Road Trip to Harvard."</li>
<li>In an episode of <a href="/wiki/Bob%27s_Burgers" title="Bob's Burgers">Bob's Burgers</a>, Wag the Hog, Critter mentions he will be going up to <a href="/wiki/Laconia,_New_Hampshire" title="Laconia, New Hampshire">Laconia, New Hampshire</a>, likely for the annual motorcycle week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents_or_natives">Notable residents or natives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable residents or natives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>See article <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_New_Hampshire" title="List of people from New Hampshire">List of people from New Hampshire</a>.</i></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Hampshire_firsts">New Hampshire firsts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=New_Hampshire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: New Hampshire firsts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>On January 5, 1776 at <a href="/wiki/Exeter,_New_Hampshire" title="Exeter, New Hampshire">Exeter</a>, the Provincial Congress of New Hampshire ratified the first independent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Constitution#1776_Constitution" title="New Hampshire Constitution">constitution</a> in the Americas, free of British rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li>On June 12, 1800, Fernald's Island in the <a href="/wiki/Piscataqua_River" title="Piscataqua River">Piscataqua River</a> became the first government-sanctioned US Navy shipyard.</li>
<li>Started in 1822, <a href="/wiki/Dublin,_New_Hampshire" title="Dublin, New Hampshire">Dublin</a>'s Juvenile Library was the first free public library.</li>
<li>In 1828, the first women's strike in the nation took place at <a href="/wiki/Dover,_New_Hampshire" title="Dover, New Hampshire">Dover's</a> Cocheco Mills.</li>
<li>Founded in 1833, the <a href="/wiki/Peterborough,_New_Hampshire" title="Peterborough, New Hampshire">Peterborough</a> Town Library was the first public library, supported with public funds, in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li>On August 3, 1852, <a href="/wiki/Center_Harbor,_New_Hampshire" title="Center Harbor, New Hampshire">Center Harbor</a> was the site of the first intercollegiate athletic event. <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale</a> in a 2-mile (3.2 km) rowing race on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipesaukee" title="Lake Winnipesaukee">Lake Winnipesaukee</a>, the first meeting in a rivalry that continues to this day.</li>
<li>Finished on June 27, 1874, the first trans-Atlantic telecommunications cable between Europe and America stretched from Balinskelligs Bay, Ireland, to <a href="/wiki/Rye,_New_Hampshire" title="Rye, New Hampshire">Rye, New Hampshire</a>.</li>
<li>On February 6, 1901, a group of nine conservationists founded the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_the_Protection_of_New_Hampshire_Forests" title="Society for the Protection of New Hampshire Forests">Society for the Protection of New Hampshire Forests</a>, the first forest-conservation advocacy group in the US.</li>
<li>In 1908, Monsignor <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Hevey" title="Pierre Hevey">Pierre Hevey</a> organized the nation's first <a href="/wiki/Credit_union" title="Credit union">credit union</a>, "La Caisse Populaire, Ste-Marie" (The People's Bank) in Manchester, to help mill workers save and borrow money, which is now St. Mary's Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1933 the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=League_of_New_Hampshire_Craftsmen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="League of New Hampshire Craftsmen (page does not exist)">League of New Hampshire Craftsmen</a> held the first <a href="/wiki/Craft" title="Craft">crafts</a> fair in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>In July 1944, the <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system" title="Bretton Woods system">Bretton Woods Agreement</a>, the first fully negotiated system intended to govern monetary relations among independent nation-states, was signed at the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington_Hotel" title="Mount Washington Hotel">Mount Washington Hotel</a>.</li>
<li>On May 5, 1961, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard" title="Alan Shepard">Alan Shepard</a> of <a href="/wiki/Derry,_New_Hampshire" title="Derry, New Hampshire">Derry</a> rode a Mercury spacecraft and became the first American in space.</li>
<li>In 1963, New Hampshire's legislature approved the nation's first modern state <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Lottery" title="New Hampshire Lottery">lottery</a>, which began play in 1964.</li>
<li>In 1966, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ralph_Baer" title="Ralph Baer">Ralph Baer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sanders_Associates" title="Sanders Associates">Sanders Associates</a>, Inc., Nashua, recruited engineers to develop the first home video game.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christa_McAuliffe" title="Christa McAuliffe">Christa McAuliffe</a> of Concord became the first private citizen selected to venture into space. She perished with her six space shuttle <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">Challenger</a></i> crewmates on January 28, 1986.</li>
<li>On May 17, 1996 New Hampshire became the first state in the country to install a green <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LED</a> <a href="/wiki/Traffic_light" title="Traffic light">traffic light</a>. New Hampshire was selected because it was the first state to install the red and yellow variety statewide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li>On May 31, 2007, New Hampshire became "...the first state to <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_New_Hampshire" title="LGBT rights in New Hampshire">recognize same-sex unions</a> without a court order or the threat of one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
